### Post by MichealH on 2010-03-30
Ok its around 18 hours until April Fools in New Zealand! Ok here goes the usual drill:

Rules:

> 1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE this is optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

[COLOR="Red"]**Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.**[/COLOR]

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-04-01
> **BwackNinja said:**
> I've had trouble finding a better font to use, this is one of my best choices (its completely readable at that size) and using fonts bigger seems weird. Any suggestions? Fonts are GE Inspira and Lucida Sans.

Although it's kind of limiting, in that it's a boldface-only font, LucidaMacBold looks pretty good, has pretty compact spacing and is highly legible at 7pt w/ antialiasing and no hinting. It's in my screenshot a page or two back, visible in the RSS feeds, xpad and any dialogue windows, if any were included in the shot. Segoe Semibold also handles itself pretty well. LucidaMAC looks okay until you come across an application that likes to use bold text, at which point it looks retarded. Lucida Sans Demibold looks good but again, like LucidaMacBold and Segoe Semibold, it's only a bold font.

Alternatively, you can go 8pt and check out the wide range of Futura fonts (although medium-weight is most legible). They've generally got a pretty low profile so they ought to avoid looking weird on your monitor.

If you have any trouble finding these fonts, just PM me.

---

### Post by BwackNinja on 2010-04-02
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Although it's kind of limiting, in that it's a boldface-only font, LucidaMacBold looks pretty good, has pretty compact spacing and is highly legible at 7pt w/ antialiasing and no hinting. It's in my screenshot a page or two back, visible in the RSS feeds, xpad and any dialogue windows, if any were included in the shot. Segoe Semibold also handles itself pretty well. LucidaMAC looks okay until you come across an application that likes to use bold text, at which point it looks retarded. Lucida Sans Demibold looks good but again, like LucidaMacBold and Segoe Semibold, it's only a bold font.

Alternatively, you can go 8pt and check out the wide range of Futura fonts (although medium-weight is most legible). They've generally got a pretty low profile so they ought to avoid looking weird on your monitor.

If you have any trouble finding these fonts, just PM me.

I tried your suggestions, but I basically went full circle with the fonts. Lucida Sans looks just about like Lucida Mac, only it is much more compressed vertically. (Lucida Mac has retarded amounts of vertical spacing, and I like to be able to display as much as possible with my RSS feed, lyrics, etc. I tried replacing my use of GE Inspira, and futura has a lot of the same kind of characters, but doesn't really look as good in my opinion (using GE Inspira at size 8, looks great for me at any hinting other than none. LucidaMacBold suffers from the same lack of vertical conservation, but I can't say I like it at sizes 8+. I've changed my tooltips to use it though, and it looks wonderful. I've changed my small font size from 6.5 to 6.6, which has slightly better spacing.

I edited my .fonts.conf more and made Lucida MAC go to LucidaMacBold when bold.

```

...
 <match target="pattern" >
  <test name="family" qual="any" >
   <string>Lucida MAC</string>
  </test>
  <test name="weight" compare="more_eq">
   <int>140</int>
  </test>
  <edit mode="assign" name="family" >
   <string>LucidaMacBold</string>
  </edit>
 </match>
...

```

The new style tooltips look really nice when theres a good amount of contrast (read: all of it). Its too bad that firefox doesn't use native tooltips.

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/attachment.php?attachmentid=152146&stc=1&d=1270182096[/IMG]

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-04-02
> **matty-guy said:**
> Question for anyone who is familiar with gtk themeing. When I highlight text then it disappears because the highlight is black and the the text goes black. How do I change this in the file?Should be text[ACTIVE] and text[SELECTED] in the relevant style. For togglebuttons, you need to add a gtkbutton*gtklabel match, although this won't always work and may screw up gtkcheckbuttons.

> **BwackNinja said:**
> I tried your suggestions, but I basically went full circle with the fonts. Lucida Sans looks just about like Lucida Mac, only it is much more compressed vertically. (Lucida Mac has retarded amounts of vertical spacing, and I like to be able to display as much as possible with my RSS feed, lyrics, etc. I tried replacing my use of GE Inspira, and futura has a lot of the same kind of characters, but doesn't really look as good in my opinion (using GE Inspira at size 8, looks great for me at any hinting other than none. LucidaMacBold suffers from the same lack of vertical conservation, but I can't say I like it at sizes 8+. I've changed my tooltips to use it though, and it looks wonderful. I've changed my small font size from 6.5 to 6.6, which has slightly better spacing.

I edited my .fonts.conf more and made Lucida MAC go to LucidaMacBold when bold.

```

...
 <match target="pattern" >
  <test name="family" qual="any" >
   <string>Lucida MAC</string>
  </test>
  <test name="weight" compare="more_eq">
   <int>140</int>
  </test>
  <edit mode="assign" name="family" >
   <string>LucidaMacBold</string>
  </edit>
 </match>
...

```

The new style tooltips look really nice when theres a good amount of contrast (read: all of it). Its too bad that firefox doesn't use native tooltips.

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/attachment.php?attachmentid=152146&stc=1&d=1270182096[/IMG]

Adding the following to your userChrome.css will fix tooltips in pages and the bookmarks menu but not in firefox's toolbars.

```
tooltip
{
	background-color: #ff0000 !important;
	font-family: LucidaMacBold !important;
	font-size: 10pt !important;
}
```

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-04-03
> **rJ~ said:**
> What clutter are you thinking of? I use most of the stuff in the panel and dock pretty often. I did remove dock icons for applications that aren't running, since I pretty much launch everything with gnome-do anyway.It's mostly the top panel. To a lesser degree, the fat bottom dock/panel. AWN supports gnome menu and tray plugins, IIRC so the top panel looks redundant from the get-go. 

The multi-coloured CPU/MEM monitors aren't helping, either. Perhaps try giving them a more fitting colour scheme, or scrapping them and using conky instead, which is far more flexible and powerful.

Probably won't show up that well on this light forum but:

[img]http://img64.imageshack.us/img64/8611/conky.jpg[/img]

The CPU/MEM stuff can be achieved with just a couple of lines, or one line, if you don't intend to superimpose the text over the graphs/bars. If you're unfamiliar with conky, just send me a PM. 

> **staar said:**
> mine for this month..

[[img]http://omploader.org/vNDEyMA[/img]](http://staarbreaker.deviantart.com/art/trigo-159303924)

Fantastic, although I'm never sure how I feel about being removing the distinctive *box panel arrows, largely useless as they are.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-04-03
Umm, where *is* your statusbar?

---

### Post by sertse on 2010-04-03
Opera allows you to enable/disable certain toolbars. This one is called the "statusbar", and it's the thinnest toolbar. I removed all status things from statusbar, added the usual navigation stuff to it instead and moved the statusbar to be on top. 

I suppose it really a "navigation bar" now, but it's still technically the statusbar.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-04-03

### Post by darthmob on 2010-04-03
> **sertse said:**

As this is a desktop screenshots thread I added that one as well. Wallpaper is from wulffmorgenthaler.com.

### Post by xc3RnbFO8P on 2010-04-04
Docky
Home made Emerald Theme
Wallpaper from Wallbase, 3107
Conky in the window

```
# UBUNTU-CONKY
# A comprehensive conky script, configured for use on
# Ubuntu / Debian Gnome, without the need for any external scripts.
#
# Based on conky-jc and the default .conkyrc.
# INCLUDES:
# - tail of /var/log/messages 
# - netstat connections to your computer
#
# -- Pengo (conky@pengo.us)
#

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,skip_taskbar
background yes

# Use double buffering (reduces fli4cker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# fiddle with window
use_spacer yes
use_xft yes

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 350

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Text stuff
draw_outline no
# amplifies text if yes
draw_borders no

uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 0

# border margins
border_margin 0

# border width
border_width 0

# Default colors and also border colors, grey90 == #626262
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color grey90

own_window_colour 080d14
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
gap_x 1250
gap_y 400

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

override_utf8_locale yes
xftfont Terminus:size=8
xftalpha 0.8

color0	ffffff	#blanco
color2	36609A	#naranjo

TEXT
${goto 10}${voffset 1}${color0}${font Musicelements:size=8}${font ArtBrush:Bold:size=8}${if_running rhythmbox} ${exec rhythmbox-client --no-start --print-playing-format %ta} - ${exec rhythmbox-client --print-playing-format %tt} ${hr 2}
${goto 10}${font ArtBrush:size=7} ${color2}Album: ${color0}${exec rhythmbox-client --no-start --print-playing-format %at} ${color2}Genero: ${color0}${exec rhythmbox-client --no-start --print-playing-format %ag} ${color2}Anho: ${color0}${exec rhythmbox-client --no-start --print-playing-format %ay} 
${goto 10}${color2} Posicion: ${color0}${exec rhythmbox-client --no-start --print-playing-format %te} ${color2}Tiempo: ${color0}${exec rhythmbox-client --no-start --print-playing-format %td}${else}${font ArtBrush:size=11:bold}${color2}Sin Actividad${font}${endif}
```

[[IMG]http://imgur.com/hHPKKl.jpg[/IMG]](http://imgur.com/hHPKK.jpg)


Back to besping huh? :P is that calendar part of the wp or is it something else?.

Heres mine... still as simple as I can, the task manager's grouping feature is so nice I am surely not coming back to bespin's xbar. Wished to use a dock-something as well but since I only used docks to put launchers in them, I stayed with a short panel with some custom icons in it.

Plasma theme is Nano with Aya's color scheme and Uniq's clock. Icons are allgrey and the color scheme is oxygen-molecule for maximmum integration with gtk+. Windeco is oxygen of course, the only one that can run nose to nose with bespin. 

The custom icons are from the token suite.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-04-05
A post for the heck of it. Having fun with how lighter ubuntu can be than normal without sacrificing any functionality. Here I run ubuntu with compiz and the likes and rtorrent, cmus and empathy running, plus all those panel applets with 170mbytes of ram (and an uptime of about 10 hrs). Add midori and a nautilus window to that and we get to 220mbytes of ram. How can then vanilla ubuntu be starting up with 300+ mbytes as some people say is beyond me. Gnome can be light (and much lighter than this if you get rid of some polish).

[[img]http://omploader.org/tNDJjcw[/img]](http://omploader.org/vNDJjcw) [[img]http://omploader.org/tNDJjdQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vNDJjdQ)

### Post by Chemical Imbalance on 2010-04-06
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> 

*breathes deeply*

Because sometime between Digg switching to a general news format and the US primaries coming to a close, the idiocy become too much to bear. The whole site basically became a clusterf*** of crackpots proselytising about the evils of climate science, the UFO cover-up, the 'green socialists', and the media and for 'making Ron Paul look crazy' (otherwise known as 'pointing a camera in Paul's direction and pressing the on button'), among other equally depressing examples of paranoia and the political fringe. The credibility of genuine issues would subsequently go to Digg to die.That and the majority of people on the site were just ridiculously emotional, defensive, reactionary twits; trolls, at various points on the autistic spectrum and otherwise sane people, with this grandiose and polarised perspective of the world, where any article that elicited people's passions, would attract either vitriol, or these ridiculously exaggerated and inept metaphors and hypotheticals. UF's more victimising offence-feigners look like angels by comparison.

/rant
I do remember enjoying the Diggnation podcast, actually. The podcast fad kind of wore on me, however.

Sounds just like 4chan or any other comment board on the internet.
That's why I don't read Digg.

The podcast is still fun to watch though.

### Post by skrite on 2010-04-07

---

### Post by Patricrawley on 2010-04-07
```
sudo aptitude install netbook-launcher
```
Then add it to your start up applications with the command netbook-launcher
You can also launch it with alt-f2 netbook-launcher

### Post by walkerk on 2010-04-07
> **gymophett said:**
> Yeah, I want Openbox really bad. I did a minimal with Openbox before, but, I tried every possible way to get tint2 running at startup and it wouldn't work. So I just gave up. >:[

Think I may give it another try today.

How did you get yours to run at start up?

create
```

~/.config/openbox/autostart.sh

```

edit it
```

#!/bin/bash

tint2 &

#and others if necessary...

```

perms
```
chmod +x ~/.config/openbox/autostart.sh
```

logout and back in...

---

### Post by Dawei87 on 2010-04-07
to get tint 2 to start, just edit the ~/.config/openbox/autostart.sh. this is pretty much where you tell all your startup applications to run. here is mine as an example:
# Run the system-wide support stuff
. $GLOBALAUTOSTART

# Programs to launch at startup

# Programs that will run after Openbox has started
(sleep 2 && tint2) &
sh ~/.fehbg &
xcompmgr -c -f &
xscreensaver -no-splash &
mpd /home/david/.mpd/config &
(sleep 3 && conky) &
(sleep 3 && conky -d -c /home/david/.conkyrc1) &

@ walkerk: you beat me!

---

### Post by Yes on 2010-04-11
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I made this God-awful theme today which happens to be a retarded lovechild of my bank's iPhone app and my Macchiato theme.

Here's the result:

The tabs in Firefox look like buttons instead of tabs, is that because of your GTK theme or did you do something with Firefox to get them like that?  If you changed Firefox, could you tell me what you did?  They look really nice like that.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2010-04-11
> **Yes said:**
> The tabs in Firefox look like buttons instead of tabs, is that because of your GTK theme or did you do something with Firefox to get them like that?  If you changed Firefox, could you tell me what you did?  They look really nice like that.

1.  Install Stylish
2.  In the Stylish menu, click "Write New Style"
3.  Enter the following and click Save:

```
@namespace url(http://www.mozilla.org/keymaster/gatekeeper/there.is.only.xul);


.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-up,
.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-down,
.tabs-alltabs-button,
.tabs-newtab-button,
.tabbrowser-tab {
    -moz-appearance:button!important;
    margin: 1px 1px 1px 1px !important; padding:0 1px!important;}

.tabs-bottom{display:none!important;}

.tabbrowser-tab * {margin:-0px 0!important;}
.tabs-alltabs-button {padding:0!important; border:0px!important;}

.tabs-alltabs-button .toolbarbutton-menu-dropmarker {margin: 0 -2px -2px 0!important;}

.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-up .toolbarbutton-icon {margin:0 3px 0 2px!important;}
.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-down .toolbarbutton-icon {margin:0 2px 0 3px!important;}

.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-up:active .toolbarbutton-icon{margin:-1px 4px 2px 1px!important;}
.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox > .scrollbutton-down:active .toolbarbutton-icon{margin:-1px 3px 2px 2px!important;}

.tab-close-button{-moz-appearance:none!important; margin:-4px 0!important;}


```

---

I don't know about you but there's a very finite number of addons I can install, before I notice a performance drop.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2010-04-11
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Kind of unnecessary to install an addon, when you can put that straight into .mozilla/firefox/<profilename>.default/chrome/userChrome.css

I don't know about you but there's a very finite number of addons I can install, before I notice a performance drop.

It may be unnecessary for you, but I find it much simpler to use Stylish than to edit userChrome.css.  Stylish allows me to write separate styles for different websites or different aspects of the Firefox UI.  By letting me keep everything separate, I can enable and disable specific styles and delete them.  More importantly, though, it allows me to see live previews of changes I've made and allows me to apply them without having to restart the browser.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2010-04-14
> **koleoptero said:**
> You must have the most consistent desktop there is. The only thing that bothers me is the size of the notification. :lolflag:

Consistent as in never-changing, or consistent, as in carefully laid out? I'm constantly changing my desktop, it's just most of those changes are either minor visual tweaks (panel icons, more subtle dark scrollbar steppers, trying to find the right look for active buttons), or more behind-the-scenes stuff (allowing more of the core Xfce apps/dialogues to behave with a sense of entitlement, ie. always-on-top, sticky and dark, with some skipping the taskbar/becoming non-minamisable, depending upon the most-likely usage scenario; ability to dynamically resize sticky notes; new window sizes).

Even just my file managing ('browsing' is probably a more appropriate verb; all my management is done via bash) has changed rather radically in the last week or so, although it's being hampered by some of the limitations of thunar's UI (no keyboard shortcuts while the search popup is visible, for example). Even just reskinning thunar and killing the sidebar, forcing myself to use the Places panel plugin, has altered the entire feel of my desktop: making thunar less of an application 'on' my desktop and more an extension utility of the desktop environment.

And for some reason I like over-sized notifications and tooltips. Probably got something to do with them being transient and easily missed. xfce4-notifyd popups would look less fat without the rounding but without it, I end up forgetting they're there. I need the rounding to reinforce that it's not stuck to the desktop, like xpad or conky and it actually needs my attention.

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2010-04-16
Terminus is an excellent alternative as koleoptero suggested. May I know how you are trying to define the font in you panelrc? Remember fixed is a bitmap font! Foer extremely small sized fonts, you can always try artwiz package.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2010-04-16
> **matty-guy said:**
> It looks nice on dzen, but I just downloaded the 'fixedsys' font, which I assume is the same one, and tried it on bmpanel at a small size and it looks hideous.

fixedsys is (probably in this case) a TTF clone of the old Windows font of the same name.   If you want a small font that is still legible, try the above suggestion, or the artwiz fonts, gohufont, or really any PCF-type font.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-04-16
If you're using ubuntu then the Terminus font can be installed by:

sudo apt-get install xfonts-terminus* console-terminus

don't forget the *

If you're not in ubuntu then a search for just terminus should give you the proper packages. If you have installed it this way and you still don't like the way it looks then don't beat yourself over it :)

---

### Post by matty-guy on 2010-04-16
> **koleoptero said:**
> If you're using ubuntu then the Terminus font can be installed by:

sudo apt-get install xfonts-terminus* console-terminus

don't forget the *

If you're not in ubuntu then a search for just terminus should give you the proper packages. If you have installed it this way and you still don't like the way it looks then don't beat yourself over it :)

I tried the repos one but I just couldn't make it work. I know I shouldn't beat myself up over it but after being pretty much trouble free for my whole Linux life, when I do run into a problem it gets frustrating. I'm sure everyone here can relate.

### Post by ayoli on 2010-04-18
> **mcoleman44 said:**
> Anyway to do it in gnome? I know you can do it with opacity settings in Compiz, but you have to list all of the windows you want it applied to. Is there a way to apply it to all windows?

Yes, in opacity settings, create a rule with "any" (without quotes) in windows field and then set the opacity you want for all windows.

### Post by matty-guy on 2010-04-18
> **hammad1337 said:**
> May I know whats that clock in the bottom-right corner?

Nice little conky script provided by mahatanman*insert number I cant remember* of Arch forums. 

```
own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
# desktop normal override dock , when "own_window" is 'yes'
#own_window_transparent yes
own_window_colour 303030
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
own_window_argb_visual yes
own_window_argb_value 224

text_buffer_size 2048
double_buffer yes
update_interval 1
if_up_strictness address

alignment bottom_right

gap_x 3
gap_y 16

draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no

use_xft yes
xftfont monofur:size=9
# 74 12
xftalpha .1

uppercase no
default_color ffffff
color1 222222
color2 888888
color3 5D5D5D

TEXT

${voffset -8}${alignc}${time %d %B %Y}
${color3}${hr}
${alignc}${color}I T${color1} L${color} I S${color1} A S T I M E
${alignc}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 35}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 15}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 20}${color}${endif}${endif}A${color1} C${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 15}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 20}${color}${endif}${endif} Q U A R T E R${color1} D C

${alignc}${else}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 45}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 50}${color}${endif}${endif}A${color1} C${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} >= 45}${if_match ${exec date +"%M"} < 50}${color}${endif}${endif} Q U A R T E R${color1} D C

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-04-18
> **The Real Dave said:**
> In looking like a Mac? Not meant to, I just like the controls :) I'm thinking about editing it to make all the colors match a bit better, but I make the time spent worth it.
I have nothing against copying stuff from macosx, I was using elementary for quite some time lol. It's just that it doesn't seem to quite fit with the gtk in my eyes. But that's just my opinion, if it works for you then you should stick to it. :)
> **fatfranko said:**
> I like this!  May I ask how you went about this?  I want my lappy to look like this!  :)
It's ubuntu lucid lynx. The DE is Gnome. Further details:
[LIST]
[*]GTK theme is smooth unity, from [this package]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Unified1.0?content=109391") with custom colours that you can grab from the shots (lots of black).
[*]Metacity is AnyColorYouLike (gnome-look.org)
[*]Icons are AnyColorYouLike, color white, folder type 2 (you'll see what I'm talking about when you download them) (gnome-look.org)
[*]Dock is AWN with two expanders, cairo menu, and for the theme click customize, and put everything 100% transparent, and only the inner and outer borders with the colour you see.
[*]Font is sansation (google) size 7 everywhere, except for the terminal where it's consolas size 7 (liberation mono looks good too).
[*]To get the purple (or whatever) glow, install and open compizconfig-settings-manager (CCSM), and go to where it says about window decorations. There it allows you to set the colour of the shadows. Make it colourful. ;)
[*]I've also killed gnome-panel by doing "sudo chmod -x /usr/bin/gnome-panel" and to get a run dialogue I installed gmrun and added it to the commands in CCSM with a key shortcut of alt+f2.
[/LIST]

Wallpaper follows, if you need any other detail let me know. :) I have to warn you though that all that black has its usability problems (invisible scrollbars and other elements).

[[img]http://omploader.org/tNDc4NA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vNDc4NA)

---

No actually, I agree with you completely, the silvers are just that bit off >.< When I've a spare minute I'll try to get them closer matching, and change the buttons colours too :)

---

### Post by mcoleman44 on 2010-04-19
Ok, so heres another question. As you know, if you make the menus transparent the text is also transparent. Is there away to keep the text and highlighted text opaque?

---

### Post by BwackNinja on 2010-04-19
@mcoleman44

This is stuff you'd want to do in the gtk engine. With a theme that uses the murrine engine and gtk widgets that support rgba, the background would be transparent but the text would always be opaque. There isn't support for this yet completely in gtk. It should be done by Ubuntu 10.10 Maverick Meerkat.

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2010-04-19
> **skrite said:**
> looks awesome. 
I would really like your text theme or Xdefaults, 
however it is you are getting your colors

.Xdefaults is all you need for colors. Apart from that for a text editor like vim or emacs, you can use different color schemes. What you see on his screen however is just the inbuilt default emacs color scheme that would enable syntax highlighting for different types of code with font-lock-mode.

### Post by mmesantos1 on 2010-04-20
> **fontis said:**
> Could I have the details on that? It's amazing how you got it looking like that :$

Here is the info on that setup. 

GTK: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/The+Days+of+Grays?content=122249](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/The+Days+of+Grays?content=122249)
Icon: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ubuntu-X+Matt+Lynx+Iconsets+by+mickyz?content=123240](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Ubuntu-X+Matt+Lynx+Iconsets+by+mickyz?content=123240)
Wallpaper: [http://nucu.ro/displayimage.php?album=4&pos=39](http://nucu.ro/displayimage.php?album=4&pos=39)
Skydome: [http://nucu.ro/displayimage.php?album=3&pos=35](http://nucu.ro/displayimage.php?album=3&pos=35)
Dock: AWN from Ubuntu 10.04 Beta2. / Place position on the screen setting all the way to the right in Preferences, set style to edgy, theme is Dark theme which is pre-installed in AWN.
I hope I did not forget anything. ;smile

Edit: The clock is Cairo clock with default theme.

Keep in mind I am running Ubuntu 10.04 Beta 2.

### Post by pelle.k on 2010-04-20
My first dark setup really. Kinda like it.
I've moved the launchers to the center of the top panel as to not be in the way of gnome-globalmenu. I wish one could group put panel items and have them center automatically, but this will do for now.
Another odd thing is the placement of the "main menu" at the left (!), but i figured it's just an applet as any other applet, so why not. It would be nice if one could use images instead of the mandatory "Applications Places System" though.
The clock has a custom format string.
The gtk is modified to fit with the slightly lighter gray of the "dust" metacity.

[LIST]
[*]GTK - "The days of grays" (gnome-look.org)
[*]Metacity - "Dust"
[*]Wallpaper - "Trance Waves" by ArgeWorks (deviantart)
[/LIST]

[[IMG]http://imgur.com/r4zaIl.jpg[/IMG]](http://imgur.com/r4zaI.jpg)

[[IMG]http://imgur.com/I60oql.jpg[/IMG]](http://imgur.com/I60oq.jpg)

[[IMG]http://imgur.com/Adi1bl.jpg[/IMG]](http://imgur.com/Adi1b.png)

---

### Post by mmesantos1 on 2010-04-20
> **jaco223 said:**
> mmesantos1 I'm not seeing where to set 'not extend' in panel properties.

Right click on an open part of the gnome panel then go to properties under the first tab it shows expand. Make sure this is not checked.

---

### Post by pelle.k on 2010-04-20
> **matty-guy said:**
> Looks good. What tiler are you using?

I wrote my own, using shell script using wmctrl. I haven't posted in anywhere yet, because it's kinda rough, and a "work in progress". You got to manually feed it some variables about your desktop such as window deco thickness, resolution, panel margins, title bar height etc.
It's got four corners set up in a 40/60 ratio, and left right (also 40/60), and a fullscreen mode. All windows respect a margin in all directions, as well as individual margins in all directions (for dodging panels and such).

I run it with xbindkeys bound to the numpad keys. Here you go;
[http://downloads.tuxfamily.org/pandora/temp/wcontrol/](http://downloads.tuxfamily.org/pandora/temp/wcontrol/)

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-04-20
> **mcoleman44 said:**
> Would you mind explaining how you got it looking like this? Include the kicks and punches, Im always looking for a fight with my lappy! :)
Nautilus elementary for lucid [from here.]("http://www.webupd8.org/2010/04/install-nautilus-elementary-230-in.html") Then go to preferences and tinker with them (it has some extra on the last tab, or you can find them with gconf-editor).
GTK theme is elementary mod (gnome-look.org)
Icons are Meliae SVG dark, with some from the older meliae for the dock. (both on gnome-look)
Metacity is aurora-aln (gnome-look) but I'm still looking for the perfect one lol.
I use a custom semitransparent background for the panel, after I commented out the panel_bg line from the theme's gtkrc file.
Dock is awn with custom colours (the gtk colours but more transparent). Also install gnome-globalmenu from their ppa.
Wallpaper from [somewhere in here.]("http://profesorul09.webs.com/apps/photos/")
The punches and kicks were because I had messed a lot of configs and I had to find the nautilus prefs the hard way. lol
> **hhh said:**
> Bing looks awesome today. Sorry, anti-MS people...
I agree bing looks awesome. And not just today.

gtk-icon-sizes = "panel-menu=16,16:panel=16,16:gtk-menu=16,16\
:gtk-large-toolbar=20,20:gtk-small-toolbar=16,16:gtk-button=18,18"

here is mine:

### Post by NightwishFan on 2010-04-22
The shell is pretty stable. It might be a bit slow at this stage but it definitely is very usable, if you want to install run this command:
```
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:ricotz/testing && sudo aptitude update && sudo aptitude safe-upgrade && sudo aptitude install gnome-shell
```

Then push alt+f2 and run:
```
gnome-shell -r
```

### Post by murderslastcrow on 2010-04-23

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-04-23
> **BslBryan said:**
> I love it.
Thanks. :)
> **Ringi said:**
> Details koleoptero, details... 
:) love it
It's [all the stuff I listed here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9151440&postcount=845"), apart from the wall that was posted a couple of pages ago by mrdiego. The dock is awn, set to curved and almost completely transparent (gradient 2 is white with 32 transparency), placement top (yeah) and at the advanced preferences set to monitor mode and the y-offset to whatever it takes to get it to the border of the wall (mine is 680somenthing). Panel on top is gnome-panel with a custom background which I'm ttaching here. To get properly transparent you need to edit the theme's gtkrc file and remove the panel_bg line (comment it out).
Also in nautilus set the toolbar to be vertical and not horizontal and the default zoom to 66% (much more workable imho). Metacity is the old elementary, I hate the new one with a passion, it's got no style whatsoever. Fonts are Aller 8 everywhere.

What's even better with this kind of setup is that you can (I have) set the bottom corners to do things with compiz, like expo and scale-switcher, so that you can move between windows and workspaces without using any panel, and you can show the desktop by moving the mouse to the scale corner and then clicking anywhere that's not a window. Very convenient.

Anyway I seem to be in a talking mood so I'll shut up before this post becomes a four book novel.

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-04-24
A different take on yesterday's theme.
This one is basically 1 f-stop less saturated/darker. Contrast might be a little low for most folk, but it works well for me. Also smudged up a simple wallpaper with my airbrush pen and GIMP brushes to match.

[[IMG]http://img215.imageshack.us/img215/3007/201004241935021024x600s.png[/IMG]]("http://omploader.org/vNDlncA")



@matty-guy (and anyone else that wants it)

Pack is ready.
Download = [http://www.mediafire.com/?mun2zymimio](http://www.mediafire.com/?mun2zymimio)
 
Archive contains 2 themes (this screenshot + the one you wanted from yesterday), 2 alternative GTKs, 2 tint2rc configs, and 2 wallpapers (this one and the plain #121313 one). There's also a badly worded "Details.txt" document that explains some additional stuff, so please read that first.
Additional notes = [http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/post/65657/#p65657](http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/post/65657/#p65657)

Cheers.

### Post by phredbull on 2010-04-24
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> no, no. i really have no idea what it means. dude, i'm serious!
File compression (as related to images and sounds) means reduction in file size, at the expense of detail; more compression = smaller file w/more pixelation/artifacts. Some compressed formats leave more obvious artifacts than others.

### Post by stanca on 2010-04-27
> **mcoleman44 said:**
> @stanca,
Mind sharing your conky script??
No,I dont.;)Here it is,just edit it to your needs::)
 > # FEDORA-CONKY

 
background yes

use_xft yes

xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=7

xftalpha 0.8

out_to_console no

update_interval 2.0

total_run_times 0

own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
own_window_transparent yes

double_buffer yes

draw_shades no

draw_outline no

draw_borders no

draw_graph_borders no

stippled_borders 0

border_inner_margin 10

border_width 2

default_color white
default_shade_color white
default_outline_color white

minimum_size 5 5
maximum_width 256

alignment top_right

gap_x 5
gap_y 5

no_buffers yes

uppercase no

cpu_avg_samples 1

net_avg_samples 1

override_utf8_locale yes

use_spacer right


TEXT
       ${color #888888}$sysname $kernel on Amd64
       Uptime: $uptime$color

                ${font :size=10}${time %a. %b. %d, %G}$font
               ${font :size=20:bold}${time %H:%M:%S}$font

       ${voffset -5}${color #888888}${hr 1}$color$voffset
        ${freq cpu0} MHz${alignr}$loadavg
${voffset -8}${alignr}${cpugraph 25,200 000000 ff0000}$voffset
${color red}${font :size=13}${alignr}${cpu cpu0}%$font$color
       ${voffset -10}${color green}GPU Temp: ${color purple}${execi 60 nvidia-settings -query GPUCoreTemp | perl -ne 'print $1 if /GPUCoreTemp.*?: (\d+)./;'}°C$voffset
      ${color #888888}${hr 1}$color
${color green}${alignr}${membar 11,120}$color
       ${voffset -11}$memperc%  RAM used: $mem${alignr}${offset 10}${color #888888}/$color$memmax$offset$voffset
${color green}${alignr}${swapbar 11,120}$color
       ${voffset -11}$swapperc% Swap used: $swap${alignr}${offset 10}${color #888888}/$color$swapmax$offset$voffset
           Cache used: $cached
      ${color #888888}${hr 1}$color
${offset 65}${color #888888}Processes: $color$processes 	${color #888888}Running: $color$running_processes$offset
${voffset -8}$voffset

       ${color green}NAME              PID   CPU    MEM
       ${top name 1}  ${top pid 1}${top cpu 1} ${top mem 1}
       ${top name 2}  ${top pid 2}${top cpu 2} ${top mem 2}
       ${top name 3}  ${top pid 3}${top cpu 3} ${top mem 3}
       ${top name 4}  ${top pid 4}${top cpu 4} ${top mem 4}
       ${top name 5}  ${top pid 5}${top cpu 5} ${top mem 5}
       ${top name 6}  ${top pid 6}${top cpu 6} ${top mem 6}
       ${top name 7}  ${top pid 7}${top cpu 7} ${top mem 7}
       ${top name 8}  ${top pid 8}${top cpu 8} ${top mem 8}
       ${top name 9}  ${top pid 9}${top cpu 9} ${top mem 9}
      ${color #888888}${hr 1}

      ${voffset -5}${color green}Root: $color${fs_free /}${color #888888}${font :size=7}free$font${alignr}${color red}${diskio /dev/sdb10}$color$voffset
        ${color #333333}${fs_bar 11,208 /}$color${offset -205}${font :size=7}${fs_used /}$font$offset
${alignr}${voffset -12}${diskiograph /dev/sdb10 11,155 333333 ff0000}$voffset
${alignc}${color purple}${offset 20}${execi 60 hddtemp /dev/sdb | cut -c32-36;}$offset$color
      ${color green}Home: $color${fs_free /home}${color #888888}${font :size=7}free$font${alignr}${color red}${diskio /dev/sdb10}$color
        ${color #333333}${fs_bar 11,208 /home}$color${offset -205}${font :size=7}${fs_used /home}$font$offset
${alignr}${voffset -12}${diskiograph /dev/sdb10 11,155 333333 ff0000}$voffset

${alignr}${voffset -12}${diskiograph /dev/sdb 11,155 333333 ff0000}$voffset
${alignc}${color purple}${offset 20}${execi 60 hddtemp /dev/sdb | cut -c24-28;}$offset$color
      ${color #888888}${hr 1}$color
${alignr}(${addr eth0})
${voffset -8}$voffset
           ${font :size=8}${color red}Uploading: ${alignr}${color green}Downloading:$color$font
          ${font :size=12}${upspeedf eth0}KB/s ${alignr}${downspeedf eth0}KB/s$font
       ${color #888888}${upspeedgraph eth0 25,104 000000 ff0000} ${alignr}${downspeedgraph eth0 25,104 000000 00ff00}$color
        ${color #888888}Total: $color${totalup eth0} ${color #888888}${alignr}Total: $color${totaldown eth0}

                ${color #888888}torrent:$color ${tcp_portmon 60000 60000 count}$color ${alignr}60000
       ${color #888888}Inbound Connections ${alignr}Service/Port$color
	${tcp_portmon 1 32767 rip 0} ${alignr}${tcp_portmon 1 32767 lservice 0}
	${tcp_portmon 1 32767 rip 1} ${alignr}${tcp_portmon 1 32767 lservice 1}
       ${color #888888}Outbound Connections ${alignr}Service/Port$color
       ${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rip 0} ${alignr}${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rservice 0}
       ${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rip 1} ${alignr}${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rservice 1}
       ${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rip 2} ${alignr}${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rservice 2}
       ${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rip 3} ${alignr}${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rservice 3}
       ${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rip 4} ${alignr}${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 rservice 4}

        ${color #888888}Inbound:$color${tcp_portmon 1 32768 count}  ${color #888888}Outbound:$color${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 count} ${color #888888}${alignr}Total:$color${tcp_portmon 1 65535 count}
${font :size=8}${color yellow}syslog   ${hr 1}$color
${font :size=7}${execi 2 tail -n2 /var/log/syslog | fold -w50}
${font :size=8}${color yellow}kern.log  ${hr 1}$color
${font :size=7}${execi 2 tail -n2 /var/log/kern.log | fold -w50}$font
${font :size=8}${color yellow}messages ${hr 1}$color
${font :size=7}${execi 2 tail -n2 /var/log/messages | fold -w50}
